## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T04:15:36Z

Good catch — let me investigate. The SessionStart hook is supposed to detect resume vs fresh and inject a "RESUMED SESSION" marker only on resumes. If both coordinators are short-circuiting to "Session resumed" on fresh starts, the hook is misclassifying or the prompt instructions are misreading its output.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T04:16:37Z

Found it. Diagnosis:

**The hook is correct. The model is misreading.**

`scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` lines 22–24 explicitly bail with no output when `source=startup`:

```bash
if [ "$SRC" != "resume" ] && [ "$SRC" != "clear" ] && [ "$SRC" != "compact" ]; then
  exit 0
fi
```

It only injects the `"RESUMED SESSION — do not re-read startup files…"` sentinel on `resume|clear|compact`. On a true fresh start, no sentinel is emitted.

**What you saw in this session:** the system-reminder header was `SessionStart:startup hook success` — `startup`, not `resume`. The sentinel string `RESUMED SESSION` is *not* in the injected context. The instruction in the startup chain is unambiguous:

> if it injected "RESUMED SESSION ...", skip the reads below and reply only: "Session resumed." Otherwise read the full chain.

I (and Sona, presumably) skipped anyway. That's a prompt-following failure on the coordinator side, not a hook bug.

**Why both coordinators trip on it.** The other SessionStart hook (`inbox-watch-bootstrap.sh` / remember dump) emits a *huge* `=== REMEMBER === / === MEMORY ===` block that gets truncated to a persisted-output file. That looks "resume-flavored" — pre-loaded context, recent-history tags — and the coordinator pattern-matches on "lots of context already injected → must be a resume" instead of grepping for the literal sentinel. Both Evelynn's and Sona's startup chains share the same instruction, so the same misread reproduces in both.

**Fixes, in order of robustness:**

1. **Tighten the instruction** in both `agents/evelynn/CLAUDE.md` and `agents/sona/CLAUDE.md` startup chains to: *"Skip the reads ONLY if the literal string `RESUMED SESSION` appears in injected context. The REMEMBER/MEMORY dump is NOT a resume marker."*
2. **Make the fresh-start case emit a positive sentinel** (e.g. `FRESH SESSION — read the startup chain`) so there's no ambiguity in either direction.
3. **Move the REMEMBER/MEMORY dump behind the resume check** so it only fires on resume/compact, where its "this is continuation" framing is accurate.

Want me to dispatch Yuumi to apply (1)+(2) now? That's the cheap, durable fix; (3) is a deeper change worth a small plan.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T04:19:30Z

The shipping fix I made and the watcher's identity-resolution chain don't compose cleanly. Two-line follow-up plan:

- Patch `inbox-watch-bootstrap.sh` to also nudge on `resume|clear|compact`.
- Either (a) have the bootstrap nudge text include the explicit `STRAWBERRY_AGENT=<coord>` inline prefix that I just used, or (b) write the resolved identity to a file (`.coordinator-identity`) that the watcher reads as a fallback tier.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T04:54:29Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T05:22:32Z

Senna caught a load-bearing wiring defect — the `<!-- include: -->` marker is a build-time directive consumed by `scripts/sync-shared-rules.sh`, not a runtime include. The coordinator defs as shipped have the marker but no inlined payload, so the deliberation primitive never reaches runtime context. Lux's review-question #4 ("is it dead text?") was prescient.

- **Wiring:** `scripts/install-hooks.sh` line 101 calls `install_dispatcher "commit-msg"`, which generates `.git/hooks/commit-msg` — the dispatcher loops every `scripts/hooks/commit-msg-*.sh` and runs them in order. - **Plan:** `plans/implemented/personal/2026-04-21-commit-msg-no-ai-coauthor-hook.md` — shipped via PR #29 (`5138394`)
- **Docs:** `architecture/key-scripts.md` carries the entry

**Known gap (from Sona's transcripts on 2026-04-23):** the regex misses the `Claude Sonnet <N>` agent-id form — Jayce's `d8088bd` and Talon's `b2b8944` slipped through with `Co-Authored-By: Claude Sonnet 4.6`. Sona logged "tighten regex + port to missmp/company-os work-repo" as an Evelynn follow-up. Looks like that follow-up didn't get scheduled in the personal-side queue — worth pulling onto open-threads if it's not already there. Want me to dispatch Syndra for the regex tighten and have Sona handle the work-repo port?

## Duong — 2026-04-25T05:45:07Z

but I don't see it in @.claude/settings.json ? where and how is it triggered?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T05:45:29Z

Two separate hook layers — easy to confuse.

- **`.claude/settings.json` hooks** fire on **Claude tool events** (Bash invocation, Edit, Agent dispatch, SessionStart). Claude Code is the trigger.
- **Git hooks** at `.git/hooks/<verb>` fire on **git operations** (commit, push) regardless of who invoked them. Git is the trigger.

`commit-msg-no-ai-coauthor.sh` is a **git** hook, so it lives in the git layer. The chain:

1. `scripts/install-hooks.sh` runs once at setup. It writes a thin dispatcher script to `.git/hooks/commit-msg`.
2. The dispatcher (380 bytes, you can `cat .git/hooks/commit-msg`) loops over every `scripts/hooks/commit-msg-*.sh` and runs each in order.
3. When **anything** runs `git commit` — Claude, you in a terminal, a subagent, CI, a worktree — git itself invokes `.git/hooks/commit-msg`, the dispatcher fires the AI-coauthor check, exits non-zero on match, commit aborts.

The reason it's git-side and not Claude-side: catching it at the git layer means it works regardless of caller. If the gate were a `Bash(git commit *)` PreToolUse hook in `.claude/settings.json`, it would only block commits made through Claude tool calls. Git-side catches commits from worktrees, subagent shells, CI pipelines, and direct terminal use.

Same principle applies to the other entries in `scripts/install-hooks.sh`: `pre-commit-*.sh` (secret scanning, agent-shared-rules sync drift, package tests per Rule 14), `pre-push-*.sh` (TDD gate per Rule 12, regression test per Rule 13). Two parallel hook taxonomies, one per trigger layer.

So the fact that `commit-msg-no-ai-coauthor.sh` is absent from `.claude/settings.json` is correct by design.

- *Literal:* tighten the anti-AI-attribution rule to block all `Co-Authored-By:` (any name) + any AI marker (Claude, Anthropic, "Generated with", 🤖, "[Claude Code]", etc.) across commit messages, PR body, and PR comments — in both personal and work repos.

- *Failure if I take it too literally:* (a) blocking **all** `Co-Authored-By:` kills legitimate human pair-programming attribution — fine for personal where it's just you + agents, potentially hostile in work repo where colleagues co-author for real; (b) "or similar" is a non-exhaustive heuristic — needs an open enumeration, not a closed regex; (c) PR body/comments live in GitHub, not git — that's a CI lint surface, not a commit-msg hook surface, so two enforcement layers needed; (d) cross-concern means Sona ports the work-repo half.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T06:06:47Z

FYI to Sona landed (`52b2380e`). One pattern worth flagging:

**Yuumi force-added the inbox file** because `agents/*/inbox/` is gitignored, citing historical precedent (`6315a633`). The mechanism worked, but force-committing gitignored files defeats the gitignore — the file lives in canonical history forever, and subsequent inbox cleanup won't purge it. The gitignore exists because inbox was designed as **local-only fire-and-forget**: write the file in `agents/sona/inbox/` on the same machine, Sona's startup scan reads it, no commit needed.

If you and Sona always run from the same checkout (this laptop), force-commits are unnecessary — the local file alone is enough. If you sometimes run Sona from a different checkout, the inbox-is-gitignored design becomes wrong and the rule should change (track inboxes properly, not force-commit them ad-hoc).

This is a small architectural inconsistency, not a fire. Parking as a coordinator-level observation; can address in a separate pass.

For the immediate concern: Sona will see the FYI on her next session boot (whether by file presence or git pull, both surfaces are covered).

# /agent-ops — local agent operations

## Subcommand dispatch

`send sona "FYI from Evelynn — ping Duong on Slack at compact windows. When a clean compact window opens (in-flight reviews plateau, queue at a stable hold-state), ping Duong on Slack via the mcp__slack__notify_duong tool BEFORE running /pre-compact-save. Slack notification path is verified live (channel D0AUWGME21K, bot 'Duong's secretary'). Format: from_agent='Sona', brief one-line text noting the window is open and you're about to consolidate. Duong's reasoning: he doesn't watch the CLI continuously. Slack is faster for attention-needed moments. The notify_duong mechanism is hardcoded to his DM channel — no routing decision needed. When to ping: compact window opens (primary case); review reaches a state where Duong's input is genuinely needed; anything blocking forward motion. When NOT to ping: routine landings, merges, dispatches; sub-tasks completing inside an in-flight chain; 'nothing's blocked on you' moments. The deliberation primitive's altitude classifier still applies — classify before pinging. Slack is a status-ping or narrative-brief surface; never technical-detail. — Evelynn"` is parsed as `<subcommand> <rest...>`. Supported subcommands:

### `send <agent> <message...>`

Writes an inbox file at `agents/<agent>/inbox/<timestamp>-<shortid>.md` with the following schema (mirroring the former `message_agent` MCP tool):

```
---
from: <sender>
to: <agent>
priority: info
timestamp: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
status: pending
---

<message>
```

Sender is derived from `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set in environment. If the caller cannot be identified, the skill refuses with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exits 2.

**Steps to execute:**

1. Determine sender: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set, otherwise ask the caller to state who they are. If the caller cannot confirm, exit 2 with `agent-ops send: sender unknown`.
2. Delegate to `scripts/agent-ops/send.sh` via the Bash tool (mirrors `list` / `new` patterns). The script validates the target agent, creates the inbox directory, and writes the file — no Write tool is used, so the inbox-write guard does not fire.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/agent-ops/send.sh" "<agent>" "<sender>" "<message>"
```

3. Print the full path of the created inbox file (the script prints it on stdout).

### `list [--json]`

Shells out to `scripts/list-agents.sh` (with `--format json` if `--json` is given) via Bash and prints the result.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh"
# or with --json flag:
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh" --format json
```

### `new <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]`

Shells out to `scripts/new-agent.sh` with the provided arguments via Bash:

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/new-agent.sh" <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]
```

## Refusal rules

- If `send sona "FYI from Evelynn — ping Duong on Slack at compact windows. When a clean compact window opens (in-flight reviews plateau, queue at a stable hold-state), ping Duong on Slack via the mcp__slack__notify_duong tool BEFORE running /pre-compact-save. Slack notification path is verified live (channel D0AUWGME21K, bot 'Duong's secretary'). Format: from_agent='Sona', brief one-line text noting the window is open and you're about to consolidate. Duong's reasoning: he doesn't watch the CLI continuously. Slack is faster for attention-needed moments. The notify_duong mechanism is hardcoded to his DM channel — no routing decision needed. When to ping: compact window opens (primary case); review reaches a state where Duong's input is genuinely needed; anything blocking forward motion. When NOT to ping: routine landings, merges, dispatches; sub-tasks completing inside an in-flight chain; 'nothing's blocked on you' moments. The deliberation primitive's altitude classifier still applies — classify before pinging. Slack is a status-ping or narrative-brief surface; never technical-detail. — Evelynn"` is empty, print the subcommand help below and exit 0.
- If the subcommand is unrecognized, refuse with `agent-ops: unknown subcommand <name>` and exit 2.
- If `send` cannot determine a sender, refuse with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exit 2.
- If `send` target agent directory does not exist, refuse with `agent-ops send: unknown agent <name>` and exit 2.

**Subcommand help (printed when arguments empty):**

```
/agent-ops <subcommand> [args]

Subcommands:
  send <agent> <message...>   Write an inbox message to an agent
  list [--json]               List all agents (TSV or JSON)
  new <agent-name> [--role]   Scaffold a new agent directory
```

## Platform note

This skill runs identically on macOS and Windows (Git Bash). All subcommands use POSIX-portable bash via the `Bash` tool — no macOS-specific commands. Agent launching is macOS-only and is handled by `scripts/mac/launch-agent-iterm.sh`; it is not available from this skill.

## Cross-references

- `architecture/platform-parity.md` — full platform support matrix
- `plans/proposed/2026-04-08-mcp-restructure.md` — rough plan (governs Phases 2–3)
- `plans/implemented/2026-04-09-mcp-restructure-phase-1-detailed.md` — this Phase 1 spec (once promoted)

## Inbox write guard

Direct `Write` or `Edit` to `agents/*/inbox/*.md` is blocked by `scripts/hooks/pretooluse-inbox-write-guard.sh` (registered as a PreToolUse hook). Use `/agent-ops send` to deliver inbox messages — this is the only sanctioned authorship path for non-admin identities. The single permitted `Edit` is the check-inbox status flip (`status: pending` -> `status: read`); all other edits are rejected. Archival moves live under `inbox/archive/` and are unguarded. Admin bypass identities: `duongntd` and `harukainguyen1411`.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T07:13:58Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T07:24:33Z

**PR #45 brief (PM-altitude):**

**Goal:** Stop subagents from committing as `Viktor <viktor@strawberry.local>` (etc.) on any worktree. Force every agent-driven commit to be authored by the neutral `Duongntd` identity, on both personal and work scopes.

**Approach so far:** A PreToolUse Bash hook that scans the shell command before execution, looking for patterns like `GIT_AUTHOR_NAME=Viktor git commit ...`, `git -c user.name=Viktor commit`, `git commit --author=Viktor`, etc. If it sees a persona name in an identity context next to a `git commit`, it blocks.

**Where it stands:**

- Senna (code quality) approved.
- Lucian (plan/ADR fidelity) keeps finding new bypasses. Latest round: **9 fresh bypasses** (NEW-BP-4 through NEW-BP-12) — line-continuation, backticks, `$(...)`, `eval "..."`, `sh -c "..."`, `bash -c "..."`, `git commit-tree`, indirect `$V` expansion. All confirmed live: each produces a `Viktor` author commit while the hook returns `exit 0`.
- **Lucian's structural critique:** the PreToolUse layer is inherently pre-`execve` — it sees shell *source*, not the resolved values. Every regex fix opens the door for another level of indirection. He's saying: stop chasing this at the input layer.

**Lucian's recommended pivot (Option A):**

- Move enforcement to a **`pre-commit` hook** that reads `git var GIT_AUTHOR_IDENT` / `GIT_COMMITTER_IDENT`. By then all shell expansion is done; git has resolved the final author. One regex against the resolved string catches every bypass above.
- Pair with a **client-side `pre-push`** (or server-side `pre-receive`) that does `git cat-file commit <sha>` to catch `git commit-tree` (which skips `pre-commit`).
- Keep the shlex/PreToolUse scanner as defense-in-depth, not the primary gate.

**Why the architectural split matters:** Lucian's argument is that the hook is "trying to be a partial shell interpreter, and that's an unbounded problem." A resolved-identity check sees ground truth — what git is *actually about to record*. The PreToolUse scanner sees skeletons.

**Decision needed:**

1. How to proceed with PR #45?
   a: pivot to Option A (pre-commit + pre-push reading resolved identity); land partial improvement of #45 separately or close #45 in favor of a clean re-implementation
   b: take the smaller fix — patch NEW-BP-4/5/10 cheaply (whitespace-strip on `git` token, reject backtick/`$(` in identity tokens, extend commit-class to `commit-tree`), accept the rest as residual risk, file a follow-up plan
   c: close #45 entirely, accept current state until we hit a real persona-leak incident
   Pick: **a** — the bypass surface is genuinely unbounded at the current layer; Lucian's analysis is sound; the rewrite is small (a `pre-commit` hook is a few lines of bash). Worth doing now while it's hot rather than discovering a leak in the wild.

- `tools/plan-cost-rollup.sh` — joins ccusage tokens/cost + git log (phases) + plan-events stream by `(plan_path, branch, commit_sha)` → one row per plan, phase-bucketed.
- `tools/off-track-signals.sh` — pure git+gh queries: review rejections, force-pushes, plan-status backwards transitions, abandoned branches.

**The "dashboard" becomes a join + skin, not a UI:**
- Per-plan table (our script, plain text or one Grafana panel)
- Trace tree (Langfuse, free)
- Off-track signals (our script)

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T08:29:03Z

- Transcript excerpt — scripts/clean-jsonl.py lacks --since-last-compact. That's a real tooling gap;
  worth a Karma quick-lane next time the queue opens. what's this?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T08:29:48Z

**What the gap is, concretely:**

`scripts/clean-jsonl.py` turns a raw Claude Code session `.jsonl` (full of tool calls, tool results, system reminders, extended thinking) into a clean Markdown transcript that keeps **only** user prompts + assistant prose. End-session uses it to archive the conversation human-readably under `agents/<name>/transcripts/`.

Today's CLI flags (line 567-571):
- `--agent` (required)
- `--session` (jsonl filename, defaults to `auto` = newest)
- `--out` (output path)
- `--project-dir` (where the jsonls live)

There's **no way to slice the transcript at a `/compact` boundary**. The script processes the whole jsonl front-to-back.

**Why that bites pre-compact-save specifically:**

Lissandra's protocol has an optional Step 5 — emit a transcript excerpt of "what happened in this leg" so future-me can read the conversation that produced the handoff shard. But "this leg" means **since the last /compact**, not since session start. After a long session that has been compacted 3-4 times, the full cleaned transcript is mostly stale work that already got consolidated into earlier handoff shards. The useful excerpt is the tail.

**The fix would be a `--since-last-compact` flag** that walks the jsonl, finds the most recent compact marker (the harness injects an `isCompactSummary: true` entry, or the `<command-name>compact</command-name>` slash-command boundary works as a fallback), and emits only entries after that point. Maybe 30-50 lines of Python — find-the-marker + slice.

**Why it's "Karma quick-lane next time the queue opens":** It's a single-file additive change in a script outside `apps/**`, no cross-process semantics, well-scoped — exactly the trivial-task shape Karma handles. Not urgent because Lissandra correctly skipped the step rather than producing a stale or mis-sliced excerpt — fail-loud, not silent. But every pre-compact-save will keep skipping it until the flag exists, so each consolidation loses potential context fidelity.

Park it or dispatch — your call. I'd park behind the cornerstone plans and the two PR #56 fix-forwards.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T08:30:43Z

Skarner extraction complete. The doc exists at `assessments/research/2026-04-25-agent-observability-tooling.md` (173 lines). Committing so it lives on main.

```
   archived it to start fresh after Lux's research. Read it for context but
   do not feel bound to its shape.

## Architectural questions you must answer

These are open and Duong wants your judgment, not Lux's. Take a position on each.

1. Deterministic metric source — what is the canonical event log? Options:
   OTel spans, JSONL parsing, git-history, agents.json ledger, hybrid. Time
   normalization (the "strip objective factors" requirement — internet
   latency, Duong-AFK gaps) requires careful choice. Wall-clock is
   unreliable; tool-execution time minus network round-trip might be closer
   to truth; token counts are fully deterministic. Recommend a primary
   metric (probably token cost) with wall-clock as secondary annotated with
   idle-detection.

2. Plan-stage event detection — how do we deterministically map "this work
   was the Aphelios breakdown stage of plan X" vs "this was Xayah's test
   plan"? Today this attribution is implicit. Candidates: subagent-sentinel
   files, commit-message conventions (Promoted-By trailer), explicit
   plan-file frontmatter mutations as the agent advances stages, harness-
   emitted events in JSONL. Pick a discipline. May require process change.

3. Storage and query layer — Langfuse (self-hosted, complex stack:
   Postgres+ClickHouse+Redis+MinIO) is heavy; SQLite + DuckDB is light.
   What's the minimum viable storage that still answers Duong's queries?
   Bias toward minimum complexity unless you can defend the heavier stack
   with concrete query patterns it unlocks.

4. Dashboard UI — bespoke web app, Langfuse's built-in UI, Grafana with
   custom panels, or static HTML generated from a query script? Duong asked
   for "custom dashboard" but didn't specify framework. The plans-folder
   list-and-drilldown pattern is well-suited to a static HTML generator
   that re-runs after each plan-stage event. Argue for or against.

5. Cost ceiling — Duong said "$/month OK if it provides real clarity." Set
   a defensible monthly ceiling and what triggers crossing it. Free tier
   first; paid tier only if specific query patterns require it.

6. Canonical agent system v1 lock — process design, not tool design. Define
   what "canonical v1" means: which agent defs, which routing rules, which
   hooks are frozen during the measurement week. Define the weekend retro:
   who runs it, what artifacts they produce (probably a v1→v2 ADR you
   author), what triggers a non-weekend hotfix-bypass to the lock. This is
   the loop Duong actually cares about.

7. Sequencing across the three cornerstone plans — agent-feedback-system,
   coordinator-decision-feedback, and dashboard. Which ships first?
   Dashboard probably last since it consumes the events the other two emit,
   but argue your position. Each has its own approved/proposed plan; you
   may need to amend one or both to make the integration coherent.

## Deliverable

A single architectural plan at
plans/proposed/personal/2026-04-25-retrospection-dashboard-and-canonical-v1.md
with the standard frontmatter. Include:

- Executive summary (3-5 sentences max — Duong reads this first)
- Your position on each of the 7 architectural questions above
- Concrete proposed architecture (storage, ingestion, query, UI, normalization)
- Phasing — what ships in week 1 vs later
- Integration with the two approved feedback plans (sequencing + dependency edges)
- v1-lock + weekend-retro process spec
- Open questions you need Duong to answer before breakdown begins (keep these
  tight — don't over-multiply OQs)
- Risks + tradeoffs honestly stated

Length budget: aim for 200-400 lines. Do not over-write.

## Process notes

- You are advisory authority but the plan goes to proposed/, not approved/
- Do not dispatch Aphelios or any breakdown agent. Plan only.

  WebFetch / WebSearch.
- Commit your plan when done; report path + commit SHA + the 1-3 OQs you
  most need answered.

Take the time you need. This is the cornerstone of the self-improving system
loop — getting the architecture right matters more than shipping fast.
```

## Duong — 2026-04-25T09:07:53Z

/btw can you recommend me a book so I can read to know more about this? like system engineering or something like that

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T09:10:21Z

Slack ping landed. Now your book question — taking it seriously because the system you're building has real lineage in published thinking.

**Top pick — read this one first:**

📕 **"Designing Data-Intensive Applications" by Martin Kleppmann** (often called *DDIA*).

This is the canonical text for the exact architecture Swain just chose. The book teaches you to think in terms of **logs as the source of truth and dashboards as derived views** — which is precisely what `events.jsonl` + DuckDB + static-HTML is. It covers event sourcing, schema evolution, batch vs stream processing, and why "the log is the database" is a more powerful idea than it sounds. After reading it you'll be able to evaluate Swain's plan as an architect peer rather than as a stakeholder. ~600 pages but you can read selectively — chapters 3, 11, and 12 are the directly-relevant ones for what we're building.

**Three honorable mentions, by topic:**

1. **"Observability Engineering" by Charity Majors et al.** — directly on the *what should we measure and why* question. Coined the modern definition of observability (high-cardinality structured events) and argues against dashboards-of-aggregates in favor of slice-and-drill. Reading this would let you push back on Swain's UI-as-static-HTML choice if you decide drill-down matters more than he weighted it.

2. **"Accelerate" by Forsgren / Humble / Kim** — the empirical research behind DORA metrics (deployment frequency, lead time, change-fail rate, MTTR). The dashboard you're commissioning is essentially DORA-for-agents. Short book (~250 pages), data-heavy, will give you vocabulary for what "performance" means quantitatively.

3. **"Thinking in Systems" by Donella Meadows** — the meta-layer. This is what makes the *v1-lock → measure → retro → v2* cycle a coherent design pattern rather than an arbitrary cadence. Feedback loops, leverage points, why systems resist change. ~200 pages, very approachable. If DDIA is the architecture textbook, this is the philosophy textbook for self-improving systems.

**My ranked read order for your specific situation:**

1. **Thinking in Systems** first (it's short, cheap, and frames everything else)
2. **DDIA** second (the heavy architectural lift)
3. **Observability Engineering** third (sharpens the dashboard critique)
4. **Accelerate** fourth (only if you want the org-performance research lens)

If you can only commit to one: DDIA. It will pay back across years, not just this dashboard.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T09:32:19Z

You're right — I misread Swain's intent. Let me stop the parallel-dispatch plan I was about to execute and ask for clarity, because there's a tension between two parts of the plan:

**§Q7 headline (strict reading):**
> Position: feedback-system → decision-feedback → dashboard, in that order
> The dashboard *consumes* events that the other two plans *emit*. Shipping it first would render empty rows.

**Swain's session-closing note (phased reading):**
> Aphelios should break down Phase 1 first; the two T.COORD.1/2 amendments are quick-lane Karma work and should land before Phase 2 begins.

The two reconcile if you separate breakdown from implementation: Phase 1 of the dashboard ("walking skeleton" — events.jsonl scanner + plan-rollup query + static HTML for one historical implemented plan) consumes only data that **already exists** today (JSONL, sentinels, git history). It doesn't need the feedback plans to ship. Phase 2 is where the dashboard needs feedback + decision events, and T.COORD.1/2 amendments must precede Phase 2.

**So the actual execution branches:**

**Option A — strict feedback-first:**
1. Aphelios breaks down `agent-feedback-system` → ship it
2. Aphelios breaks down `coordinator-decision-feedback` → ship it
3. Karma lands T.COORD.1/2 amendments (or fold into the breakdowns)
4. Aphelios breaks down dashboard → ship Phase 1 → 2 → 3

Net: dashboard render is weeks out. You don't see anything until feedback ships.

**Option B — Swain's phased reading:**
1. Aphelios breaks down `agent-feedback-system` (first, since it's the upstream)
2. **In parallel**: Aphelios breaks down dashboard Phase 1 only (the historical-data walking skeleton)
3. Karma lands T.COORD.1/2 amendments before Phase 2 starts
4. Phase 2 dashboard waits for feedback + decision plans to be in-progress

Net: you get a working dashboard rendering existing plans within ~3 sessions, while the feedback infrastructure builds in parallel. Risk: Phase 1 of dashboard is a small extra investment if the schema contracts shift, but Swain hedged that with the §Q7 amendment requirement.

**Which do you want?** I was defaulting to Option B (parallel) because Swain's session-close said it. If you meant strict feedback-first per §Q7's headline, I cancel the parallel Aphelios dashboard dispatch and queue feedback-system breakdown solo.

Orianna is still gating the dashboard-plan promotion in the background — that's fine either way, the plan being approved doesn't force immediate breakdown. Your call drives what I dispatch next.

**Honest postmortem on the mess:** I dispatched Aphelios feedback-system breakdown (inline-mode) AND Karma T.COORD amendments (inline-mode) in parallel, both editing `agent-feedback-system.md`. Both worked on the same working tree. Whichever agent ran `git commit` first swept whatever happened to be in the index at that moment. That's why T.COORD.1's §D12 ended up bundled into my OQ-resolution commit, and T.COORD.2's §3.5 ended up bundled into Orianna's promotion commit. Karma flagged this correctly. **Lesson:** never parallel-dispatch two inline-mode agents on the same file path. Sequence them, or force worktree isolation.

The good news: all the actual content is correct on main. The bad news: per-amendment git revert is now non-trivial.

§Q2 of the dashboard plan declares Orianna trailer "canonical" and frontmatter mtime "strong corroboration" but doesn't specify behavior when they **disagree on the current stage** (e.g. trailer says `approved`, but `status:` mtime shows `in-progress` 30s later from a hand-edit).

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

- **coordinator:** Evelynn (confirmed via agent-setting line at jsonl top)
- **concern:** personal (consistent across all subagent dispatches this session)

## Duong — 2026-04-25T11:23:35Z

We should fix the wording. Find another word better for slow track

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T11:23:55Z

You're right — "slow track" carries the wrong implication (serialize, throttle). The semantic we actually want:

- Coordinator dispatches and does **not** poll/prod the agents
- Coordinator does **not** seek constant user interaction (handsoff is partly there)
- Independent work fans out **in parallel by default**
- Pace stays **measured** (no skipping discipline, no chained reflex dispatches)

Candidates:

| Word | Fit | Why |
|---|---|---|
| **low-touch** | strong | Minimizes coordinator-side fussing; says nothing about parallelism |
| **async** | strong | Dispatch-and-detach; parallel is implicit |
| **deliberate** | medium | Captures measured pace but ambiguous about touch frequency |
| **background** | medium | Captures the "agents work while you wait" shape; weak on coordinator behavior |
| **quiet** | weak | Captures non-interruptive but not the dispatch shape |
| **steady** | weak | Vague |

My pick: **"low-touch async"** as the paired phrase. "Low-touch" describes coordinator behavior (don't fuss); "async" describes the dispatch shape (parallel, fire-and-forget). Together they replace "slow track" without dragging in the serialization implication.

Alternative single word if you want one: **"low-touch"** alone.

Want me to log this as a coordinator vocabulary fix into `agents/evelynn/memory/MEMORY.md` so it propagates? Sona's parallel vocabulary should match — happy to FYI her on the rename.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T11:24:16Z

Talon shipped PR #60 (`f7ec9225` xfail + `972be9a6` impl, 5 tests passing). Dispatching dual review (Senna code-quality + Lucian fidelity) per Rule 18.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T11:25:08Z

Back to your vocabulary fix — I had offered candidates: **low-touch**, **async**, **deliberate**, **background**, **quiet**, **steady**. My pick was **"low-touch async"** as a paired phrase, or **"low-touch"** alone.

You haven't picked yet. Want me to proceed with `low-touch async` and log it into Evelynn memory + FYI Sona for vocabulary parity? Or pick another from the list?

## Duong — 2026-04-25T11:25:13Z

ok but this is the important part "Pace stays measured (no skipping discipline, no chained reflex dispatches)", the handsoff mode already covers the low-touch aysnc

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T11:25:29Z

Right — handsoff already = low-touch async. The replacement for "slow track" needs to cover a **different axis**: cognitive discipline. The pause-and-verify behavior whose absence produced today's three slips (lane mismatch, missing pair-mate, missed compact-watch).

Candidates re-narrowed for *that* axis:

| Word | Fit | Why |
|---|---|---|
| **deliberate** | strong | Intentional, paused-before-act, not reflex |
| **disciplined** | strong | Names the failure mode directly (slips were discipline failures) |
| **measured** | medium | Captures pace but ambiguous about verify-step |
| **methodical** | medium | Step-by-step verification, slightly clinical |
| **patient** | weak | Pace-only, doesn't evoke verify-step |

My pick: **"deliberate"** — clean handle, pairs cleanly with handsoff (orthogonal axes: handsoff = how often you check in, deliberate = how carefully you act before dispatch).

So the paired vocabulary becomes: **"handsoff, deliberate"** replacing **"handsoff, slow track"**.

Confirm "deliberate" and I'll log it into `agents/evelynn/memory/MEMORY.md` + FYI Sona. Or pick "disciplined" if you want the failure-mode name baked into the vocabulary.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T11:26:46Z

ok. But put this where the information currently contradict @agents/memory/duong.md I believe and fix it there

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T11:27:02Z

Found the contradiction. Line 53 names the track "slow track" but its actual semantics — "cleanest option, structurally-right, no debt" — are about **deliberate choice quality**, not pace/serialization. The name implies throttle; the body describes care. Combined with the Parallelism Preference block (lines 58-68: "fire the dispatch", "max parallelism"), the wording self-contradicts.

Renaming "slow track" → "deliberate track" preserves the semantic (cleanest, structurally-right, no debt) and removes the throttle-implication.

**Senna: CHANGES_REQUESTED on PR #59** with 1 blocker + 3 important findings. Dashboard not mergeable as-is.

**Blocker:** `parseRealGitLog` splits commit blocks on `\n\n` — real git-log output has multi-paragraph commit bodies, so every multi-paragraph Orianna promotion silently loses its `Promoted-By:` trailer in production. Mock path (`RETRO_GIT_LOG_MOCK`) bypasses the bug entirely → that's why all 53 tests pass. **Real production breaks.** Fix: use `git log -z` or `%x1e` record separator. Needs regression test with synthetic real-git-log fixture.

**Important also:**
- I1: `signal_conflict` doesn't fire on two-commit rank-tie shape (matches Lucian's TP1.T4-E xfail-not-flipped finding — same gap, different angle).
- I2: per-turn stage rollup always uses dispatch-prompt-slug; the trailer signal is emitted but never consulted in rollup.

- Lucian #1: `feat:` prefix violates plan §Phase-1-cadence.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`evelynn` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `evelynn` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying `evelynn`.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T14:52:26Z

One thing I need to flag you to improve on the system pre lock: when a task is complex and you estimated it to take hours to finish, it doesn't make sense to make 1 subagent handle all of it. why? 1. subagent does not have large context window and are not optimized to run complex task nonstop. the result will be worsen the longer it runs. 2. If the task can be broken down into multiple parallel stream, it would speed up the execution by multiple factors. So ask this before dispatch: does the task take longer than 30m? Can the task be broken down into meaningful parallel streams? If both is yes, then you should probably do so. There are some exceptions though, for example when a task requires long waiting time but actually simple, like waiting for test to run etc, it wouldn't make much sense to split it. This is the job of both the Task breakdown (Aphelios/Kayn and Xayah/Caitlyn) and the coordinator critical thinking. Also the estimation of how long a task last is still heavily bloated, and we should improve on that too

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T14:52:58Z

## Duong — 2026-04-25T15:11:27Z

couple of other things I want to add to make our system more structured, these can be Azir lanes:
- We need to have a structured way to backlog and prioritize plans. Currently they are not sorted in any way, and we just do things randomly. There should be more structures in this (plan of plans). also I want a parking lot for ideas, which simply sits there and doesn't need a proposed solution yet because we don't need it yet, so I don't want to waste time and resources to break it down now and then couple weeks later find out the idea is obsolete or the plan is stale
- I want the assessment folder to also be more structurized, Currently it doesn't follow any pattern or convention. That's Lux home, let her organize it
- I want a more structured and robust QA pipeline, currently we don't even have it documented and will easily be overlooked. QA is such an important step and is the make or break point of a plan. we currently don't have a QA plan and it often happens at the very end of the cycle, which sometimes is too late because we already built everything, but then the final result after QA is not usable, then the whole things thrown away.
- I also want you to take closer look on PR reviewers guidelines, make sure they have the best tools/plugins and guidelines available to them, because this is together with QA also what ensure the final result is the one that not just work, but work securely, scalable and reliable.
- Frontend and UI/UX design is currently heavily overlooked and it's also not documented in the process. I don't want this. We also need to prioritize this. The final product should not just be a working one but also a usable one

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T16:47:50Z

when he's done, add this to the idea: for the v2 of the system, I would perhaps want a AB test or whatever it's called. Basically we should have a deterministic test of the system, how well it performs given a specific isolated environment with a test framework. with this, the goal is to determine if the system itself is improving overtime when isolated, because there can be multiple factors that can contribute to the result, not the system itself (agent can learn and adapt overtime for example, then it's not the system is better but the agent got better) I'm not a scientist but this is well designed in this field where you have a control group, to test if the test itself is setup correctly. If yes then 10/10 time with the same setup/system and the same test, it would provide the same result. then we do the test with the target system, to see how well it performs in the same environment in accordance to the other system. This is to make sure we're going in the right direction and not fool ourselves with the outcomes

## Duong — 2026-04-25T16:54:24Z

I'm not sure A/B testing is the right word. Do you know what is the right word for it?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T16:54:56Z

Your instinct on "A/B" is partly right but missing a layer. The proper terms:

**The methodology you described has two phases:**

1. **A/A test** (the "control group" / harness self-validation step) — run the same baseline system 10× on the same fixed input, expect identical results. If results vary, the harness itself is non-deterministic and can't be trusted yet. This step has a specific name: **A/A test**. It's the self-test of the test framework.

2. **A/B test** (the actual comparison) — baseline-vs-target on the same fixed input. Compare distributions or deltas.

**For the whole pattern — deterministic replay against a frozen baseline to discriminate signal-from-confound — common field-specific names:**

- **Eval harness** (LLM/AI world — what Anthropic, OpenAI, MMLU, HumanEval, etc. all use)
- **Regression benchmark suite** (perf engineering)
- **Golden test** / **snapshot test** (software testing — when comparing exact output bytes)
- **Differential testing** (when comparing two implementations on the same inputs)
- **Controlled experiment** (the science-paper formal term)

**Best single phrase for what you actually want:**

> **Deterministic eval harness with A/A validation** (the self-test) **then A/B comparison** (the system-vs-system measurement).

The "A/B" naming you already used is correct for the second step — your instinct just had the missing piece, the A/A. Want me to update the idea file to reflect this? The original captures your verbatim text but I can prepend a "terminology note" so the v2 plan author lands on the right vocabulary.

## Duong — 2026-04-25T16:56:42Z

yes update it

## Evelynn — 2026-04-25T16:57:44Z

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, refuse immediately with `end-session: agent name required — pass the agent name as an argument (e.g. /end-session evelynn)` and exit. If `` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 6b — Update open-threads.md + regenerate INDEX.md (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6 (write shard) MUST complete before Step 6b because the shard is the source for both open-threads.md and INDEX.md updates. Step 6b MUST complete before the commit step so all artifacts land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6 completes.

1. Parse the shard's `## Open threads into next session` section (or `## Open threads` section). For each thread listed:
   - If resolved/closed: remove or mark closed the matching `## <thread>` section in `agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md`.
   - If new or still-open: add or update its `## <thread>` section with the shard UUID as a pointer and a status one-liner.
   - You are the coordinator — you confirm the diff before writing. Hand-curation is the value here.
   - If `open-threads.md` does not exist yet, create it from scratch.

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md
   ```

3. Regenerate `last-sessions/INDEX.md`:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only
   ```

4. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/last-sessions/INDEX.md
   ```

If Step 6b fails partway (e.g., `--index-only` errors), the shard written in Step 6 is already staged and recoverable. Do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed with only the shard staged. Recovery path: run `bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only`, stage `INDEX.md`, and amend the next commit manually.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator (non-coordinator agents — Sonnet subagents, Lissandra standalone, etc.):** Step 6b is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 6c — Decisions rollup (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6c MUST run after Step 6b (INDEX.md already staged) and before the commit step. All four artifacts — shard, last-sessions/INDEX.md, decisions/INDEX.md, and decisions/preferences.md — land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6b completes.

1. Regenerate decisions INDEX and roll up preferences.md counts:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --decisions-only
   ```

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/decisions/INDEX.md agents/<agent>/memory/decisions/preferences.md
   ```

If Step 6c fails (e.g., no decisions/ directory yet, or `--decisions-only` errors), do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed to the commit step. The decisions rollup is not blocking for the session commit.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator:** Step 6c is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.

## Refusal posture

You are `disable-model-invocation: false`. This skill MUST only be triggered explicitly by Duong or Evelynn typing `/end-session`. It cannot auto-fire on model judgment. If Duong's intent is ambiguous, ask before firing.
